href="#cite_note-HS76-123">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Shuna,_Slate_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Shuna, Slate Islands">Shuna</a>\n</td>\n<td>Unknown\n</td>\n<td>Norse\n</td>\n<td>Possibly "sea island"<sup id="cite_ref-MaT105_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MaT105-126">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>Seunay\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Siuna</i></i>\n</td>\n<td>Gaelic <i><i lang="mga" title="Middle Irish language text">sidhean</i></i> - "fairy"<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Skye" title="Skye">Skye</a>\n</td>\n<td><i>Scitis</i><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>Pre-Celtic?\n</td>\n<td>Possibly "winged isle"<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>Skye\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">An t-Eilean Sgitheanach</i></i>\n</td>\n<td>Numerous - see above\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Soay,_Skye" title="Soay, Skye">Soay</a>\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">So-\xc3\xb8y</i></i>\n</td>\n<td>Norse\n</td>\n<td>sheep island\n</td>\n<td>Soa Urettil\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">S\xc3\xb2dhaigh</i></i>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Tanera_M%C3%B2r" title="Tanera M\xc3\xb2r">Tanera M\xc3\xb2r</a></i>\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Hawnar\xc3\xb8y</i></i>\n</td>\n<td>Norse\n</td>\n<td>island of the haven<sup id="cite_ref-HS195_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HS195-153">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>Hawrarymoir(?)\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Tannara M\xc3\xb2r</i></i>\n</td>\n<td>Brythonic: <i><i lang="cel" title="Celtic languages collective text">Thanaros</i></i>, the thunder god<sup id="cite_ref-HS195_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HS195-153">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tiree" title="Tiree">Tiree</a>\n</td>\n<td><i>Eth</i>, <i>Ethica</i>\n</td>\n<td>Possibly pre-Celtic\n</td>\n<td>Unknown<sup id="cite_ref-W85_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W85-98">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Tioridh</i></i>\n</td>\n<td>Norse: <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Tirvist</i></i> of unknown meaning and numerous Gaelic versions, some with a possible meaning of "land of corn"<sup id="cite_ref-W85_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W85-98">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ulva" title="Ulva">Ulva</a>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Ulv\xc3\xb8y</i>\n</td>\n<td>Norse\n</td>\n<td>wolf island<sup id="cite_ref-HS102_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HS102-154">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Ulbha</i></i>\n</td>\n<td>Ulfr\'s island<sup id="cite_ref-HS102_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HS102-154">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uninhabited_islands">Uninhabited islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Uninhabited islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dubh_artach.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Dubh_artach.jpg/350px-Dubh_artach.jpg" width="350" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Dubh_artach.jpg/525px-Dubh_artach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Dubh_artach.jpg/700px-Dubh_artach.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1180" data-file-height="713" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dubh_artach.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Dhu Heartach</i> Lighthouse, During Construction</i> by <a href="/wiki/Sam_Bough" title="Sam Bough">Sam Bough</a> (1822\xe2\x80\x931878)</div></div></div>\n<p>The names of uninhabited islands follow the same general patterns as the inhabited islands. The following are the ten largest in the Hebrides and their outliers.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Scotland#Origin_of_names" title="St Kilda, Scotland">etymology of St Kilda</a>, a small archipelago west of the Outer Hebrides, and its main island <a href="/wiki/Hirta" title="Hirta">Hirta</a>, is very complex. No <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">saint</a> is known by the name of Kilda, and various theories have been proposed for the word\'s origin, which dates from the late 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Haswell-Smith (2004) notes that the full name "St Kilda" first appears on a Dutch map dated 1666, and that it may have been derived from Norse <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">sunt kelda</i></i> ("sweet wellwater") or from a mistaken Dutch assumption that the spring <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Tobar Childa</i></i> was dedicated to a saint. (<i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Tobar Childa</i></i> is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_tautological_place_names" class="mw-redirect" title="List of tautological place names">tautological placename</a>, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Gaelic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Norse</a> words for <i>well</i>, i.e. "well well").<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The origin of the Gaelic for "Hirta"\xe2\x80\x94<i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Hiort</i></i>, <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Hirt</i></i>, or <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Irt</i></i><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94which long pre-dates the use of "St Kilda", is similarly open to interpretation. Watson (1926) offers the Old Irish <i><i lang="sga" title="Old Irish language text">hirt</i></i>, a word meaning "death", possibly relating to the dangerous seas.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Maclean (1977), drawing on an <a href="/wiki/Icelanders%27_sagas" class="mw-redirect" title="Icelanders&#39; sagas">Icelandic saga</a> describing an early 13th-century voyage to Ireland that mentions a visit to the islands of <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Hirtir</i></i>, speculates that the shape of Hirta resembles a <a href="/wiki/Stag" class="mw-redirect" title="Stag">stag</a>, <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">hirtir</i></i> being "stags" in Norse.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The etymology of small islands may be no less complex. In relation to <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Dubh_Artach" title="Dubh Artach">Dubh Artach</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Louis_Stevenson" title="Robert Louis Stevenson">R. L. Stevenson</a> believed that "black and dismal" was a translation of the name, noting that "as usual, in Gaelic, it is not the only one."<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Island\n</th>\n<th>Derivation\n</th>\n<th>Language\n</th>\n<th>Meaning\n</th>\n<th>Munro (1549)\n</th>\n<th>Alternatives\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Taransay" title="Taransay">Taransay</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Norse\n</td>\n<td>Taran\'s island<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>Tarandsay\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Scarba" title="Scarba">Scarba</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Norse\n</td>\n<td>cormorant island<sup id="cite_ref-M104_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-M94-163">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>Pabay\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hirta" title="Hirta">Hirta</a>\n</td>\n<td><i>Hirt</i>\n</td>\n<td>Possibly Old Irish\n</td>\n<td>death\n</td>\n<td>Hirta\n</td>\n<td>Numerous - see above\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Mingulay" title="Mingulay">Mingulay</a>\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Mikilay</i></i>\n</td>\n<td>Norse\n</td>\n<td>big island<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>Megaly\n</td>\n<td>"Main hill island".<sup id="cite_ref-M87_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-M87-165">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Murray (1973) states that the name \xe2\x80\x9cappropriately means Bird Island\xe2\x80\x9d.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ronay" title="Ronay">Ronay</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Norse\n</td>\n<td>rough island<sup id="cite_ref-M101_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-M101-167">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Sandray" title="Sandray">Sandray</a>\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Sandray</i></i><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>Norse\n</td>\n<td>sand island<sup id="cite_ref-M103_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-M103-148">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>Sanderay\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Wiay,_Uist" title="Wiay, Uist">Wiay</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Norse\n</td>\n<td>Possibly "house island"<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a Ear</a></i>\n</td>\n<td><i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Ceann Ear</i></i>\n</td>\n<td>Gaelic\n</td>\n<td>east headland\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_history">Natural history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Natural history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In some respects the Hebrides lack biodiversity in comparison to mainland Britain; for example, there are only half as many mammalian species.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> However, these islands provide breeding grounds for many important <a href="/wiki/Seabird" title="Seabird">seabird</a> species including the world\'s largest colony of <a href="/wiki/Northern_gannet" title="Northern gannet">northern gannets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Avian life includes the <a href="/wiki/Corn_crake" title="Corn crake">corncrake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red-throated_diver" class="mw-redirect" title="Red-throated diver">red-throated diver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_pigeon" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock pigeon">rock dove</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black-legged_kittiwake" title="Black-legged kittiwake">kittiwake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_guillemot" title="Black guillemot">tystie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_puffin" title="Atlantic puffin">Atlantic puffin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_goldeneye" title="Common goldeneye">goldeneye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagle</a> and <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_eagle" title="White-tailed eagle">white-tailed sea eagle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The last named was re-introduced to R\xc3\xb9m in 1975 and has successfully spread to various neighbouring islands, including Mull.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-174">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> There is a small population of <a href="/wiki/Red-billed_chough" title="Red-billed chough">red-billed chough</a>  concentrated on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Islay" title="Islay">Islay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colonsay" title="Colonsay">Colonsay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Red_deer" title="Red deer">Red deer</a> are common on the hills and the <a href="/wiki/Grey_seal" title="Grey seal">grey seal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Common_seal" class="mw-redirect" title="Common seal">common seal</a> are present around the coasts of Scotland. Colonies of seals are found on <a href="/wiki/Oronsay,_Inner_Hebrides" title="Oronsay, Inner Hebrides">Oronsay</a> and the Treshnish Isles.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The rich freshwater streams contain <a href="/wiki/Brown_trout" title="Brown trout">brown trout</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_salmon" title="Atlantic salmon">Atlantic salmon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_water_shrew" title="Eurasian water shrew">water shrew</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Offshore, <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Killer_whale" title="Killer whale">Killer whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basking_shark" title="Basking shark">basking sharks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porpoise" title="Porpoise">porpoises</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a> are among the sealife that can be seen.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg/220px-Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg/330px-Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg/440px-Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="429" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The open landscapes of <a href="/wiki/Benbecula" title="Benbecula">Benbecula</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Heather moor containing <a href="/wiki/Calluna" title="Calluna">ling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erica_cinerea" title="Erica cinerea">bell heather</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erica_tetralix" title="Erica tetralix">cross-leaved heath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Myrica_gale" title="Myrica gale">bog myrtle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fescue" class="mw-redirect" title="Fescue">fescues</a> is abundant and there is a diversity of Arctic and alpine plants including <a href="/wiki/Sagina" title="Sagina">Alpine pearlwort</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minuartia" title="Minuartia">mossy cyphal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Loch_Druidibeg" title="Loch Druidibeg">Loch Druidibeg</a> on South Uist is a <a href="/wiki/National_nature_reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="National nature reserve (United Kingdom)">national nature reserve</a> owned and managed by <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Natural_Heritage" title="Scottish Natural Heritage">Scottish Natural Heritage</a>. The reserve covers 1,677 hectares across the whole range of local habitats.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>  Over 200 species of flowering plants have been recorded on the reserve, some of which are nationally scarce.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> South Uist is considered the best place in the UK for the aquatic plant <a href="/wiki/Najas_flexilis" title="Najas flexilis">slender naiad</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/European_Protected_Species" title="European Protected Species">European Protected Species</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/European_hedgehog" title="European hedgehog">Hedgehogs</a> are not native to the Outer Hebrides\xe2\x80\x94they were introduced in the 1970s to reduce garden pests\xe2\x80\x94and their spread poses a threat to the eggs of ground nesting wading birds. In 2003, Scottish Natural Heritage undertook culls of hedgehogs in the area although these were halted in 2007 due to protests; trapped animals were instead relocated to the mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_island_names" title="Scottish island names">Scottish island names</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Scotland" title="Geology of Scotland">Geology of Scotland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_prehistoric_Scotland" title="Timeline of prehistoric Scotland">Timeline of prehistoric Scotland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Scotland" title="Fauna of Scotland">Fauna of Scotland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/New_Hebrides" title="New Hebrides">New Hebrides</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Scotland" title="Languages of Scotland">Languages of Scotland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Goidelic_substrate_hypothesis" title="Goidelic substrate hypothesis">Goidelic substrate hypothesis</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Insular_Celtic_languages" title="Insular Celtic languages">Insular Celtic languages</a></li>\n<li><a Awakening (Religious Revival)</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References_and_footnotes">References and footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: References and footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Rollinson (1997) states that the oldest rocks in Europe have been found "near Gruinard Bay" on the Scottish mainland. Gillen (2003) p. 44 indicates the oldest rocks in Europe are found "in the Northwest Highlands and Outer Hebrides". McKirdy, Alan Gordon, John &amp; Crofts, Roger (2007) <i>Land of Mountain and Flood: The Geology and Landforms of Scotland</i>. Edinburgh. Birlinn. p. 93 state of the <a href="/wiki/Lewisian_complex" title="Lewisian complex">Lewisian gneiss</a> bedrock of much of the Outer Hebrides that "these rocks are amongst the oldest to be found anywhere on the planet". Other non-geological sources sometimes claim the rocks of Lewis and Harris are "the oldest in Britain", meaning that they are the oldest deposits of large bedrock. As Rollinson makes clear they are not the location of the oldest small outcrop.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Murray (1973) notes that "Western Isles" has tended to mean "Outer Hebrides" since the creation of the <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Na_h-Eileanan_an_Iar_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Na h-Eileanan an Iar (UK Parliament constituency)">Na h-Eileanan an Iar</a></i> or Western Isles parliamentary constituency in 1918. Murray also notes that "Gneiss Islands" \xe2\x80\x93 a reference to the underlying geology \xe2\x80\x93 is another name used to refer to the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a>, but that its use is "confined to books".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Thompson (1968) provides a more literal translation: "Fire played in the fig-trees of Liodhus; it mounted up to heaven. Far and wide the people were driven to flight. The fire gushed out of the houses".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The transitional relationships between Norse and Gaelic-speaking rulers are complex. The <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Gall-Gh\xc3\xa0idhels</i></i> who dominated much of the Irish Sea region and western Scotland at this time were of joint Gaelic and Scandinavian origin. When Somerled wrested the southern Inner Hebrides from <a href="/wiki/Godred_II_Olafsson" class="mw-redirect" title="Godred II Olafsson">Godred the Black</a> in 1156, this was the beginnings of a break with nominal Norse rule in the Hebrides. Godred remained the ruler of Mann and the Outer Hebrides, but two years later Somerled\'s invasion of the former caused him to flee to Norway. Norse control was further weakened in the ensuring century, but the Hebrides were not formally ceded by Norway until 1266.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The transitions from one language to another are also complex. For example, many Scandinavian sources from this period of time typically refer to individuals as having a Scandinavian first name and a Gaelic by-name.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-110">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There are two inhabited islands called "Grimsay" or <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Griomasaigh</i></i> that are joined to Benbecula by a road causeway, one to the north at <a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Survey_National_Grid" title="Ordnance Survey National Grid">grid reference</a> <span style="white-space: nowrap" class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://tools.wmflabs.org/os/coor_g/?pagename=Hebrides&amp;params=NF855572_region%3AGB_scale%3A25000">NF855572</a></span> and one to the south east at <a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Survey_National_Grid" title="Ordnance Survey National Grid">grid reference</a> <span style="white-space: nowrap" class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://tools.wmflabs.org/os/coor_g/?pagename=Hebrides&amp;params=NF831473_region%3AGB_scale%3A25000">NF831473</a></span>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See above note.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Citations">Citations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Citations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
